###begin article-title 0
Influence of naturally-occurring 5'-pyrophosphate-linked substituents on the binding of adenylic inhibitors to ribonuclease a: An X-ray crystallographic study
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Present address: Department of Haematology, Cambridge Institute for Medical Research, University of Cambridge, Hills Rd, Cambridge CB2 0XY, UK
###end p 1
###begin p 2
Present address: Institute of Organic and Pharmaceutical Chemistry, National Hellenic Research Foundation, 48 Vassileos Constantinou Avenue, 11635 Athens, Greece
###end p 2
###begin p 3
Present address: School of Biosciences, University of Cardiff, Museum Avenue, Cardiff CF10 3US, UK
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 558 559 558 559 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 639 640 635 636 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 678 679 674 675 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 708 711 704 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">syn</italic>
###xml 763 764 756 757 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 840 841 829 830 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 939 940 928 929 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
Ribonuclease A is the archetype of a functionally diverse superfamily of vertebrate-specific ribonucleases. Inhibitors of its action have potential use in the elucidation of the in vivo roles of these enzymes and in the treatment of pathologies associated therewith. Derivatives of adenosine 5'-pyrophosphate are the most potent nucleotide-based inhibitors known. Here, we use X-ray crystallography to visualize the binding of four naturally-occurring derivatives that contain 5'-pyrophosphate-linked extensions. 5'-ATP binds with the adenine occupying the B2 subsite in the manner of an RNA substrate but with the gamma-phosphate at the P1 subsite. Diadenosine triphosphate (Ap3A) binds with the adenine in syn conformation, the beta-phosphate as the principal P1 subsite ligand and without order beyond the gamma-phosphate. NADPH and NADP+ bind with the adenine stacked against an alternative rotamer of His119, the 2'-phosphate at the P1 subsite, and without order beyond the 5'-alpha-phosphate. We also present the structure of the complex formed with pyrophosphate ion. The structural data enable existing kinetic data on the binding of these compounds to a variety of ribonucleases to be rationalized and suggest that as the complexity of the 5'-linked extension increases, the need to avoid unfavorable contacts places limitations on the number of possible binding modes. (c) 2009 Wiley Periodicals, Inc. Biopolymers 91: 995-1008, 2009.
###end p 4
###begin p 5
This article was originally published online as an accepted preprint. The "Published Online" date corresponds to the preprint version. You can request a copy of the preprint by emailing the Biopolymers editorial office at biopolymers@wiley.com
###end p 5
###begin title 6
INTRODUCTION
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 141 142 141 142 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b1">1</xref>
###xml 348 349 348 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b2">2</xref>
###xml 350 351 350 351 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b5">5</xref>
###xml 548 549 548 549 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b6">6</xref>
###xml 550 551 550 551 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b8">8</xref>
###xml 630 631 630 631 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b9">9</xref>
###xml 632 634 632 634 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b10">10</xref>
###xml 694 696 694 696 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b11">11</xref>
###xml 710 712 710 712 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b12">12</xref>
###xml 823 825 823 825 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b13">13</xref>
###xml 1254 1255 1254 1255 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b8">8</xref>
###xml 0 6 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">Bovine</span>
###xml 667 673 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
Bovine pancreatic ribonuclease A (RNase A; EC 3.1.27.5) has long been studied as a model of enzyme structure and function (reviewed by Raines1). It is now increasingly recognised as the archetype of an intriguing enzyme superfamily whose actions are closely linked to the evolution of vertebrates and which has undergone tremendous diversification.2-5 Many members of the superfamily have potent biological activities that are dependent on their enzymatic activity. Among these are the angiogenic and tumor-promoting activities of angiogenin (Ang),6-8 the antiviral and neurotoxic activities of eosinophil-derived neurotoxin (EDN)9,10 and the cytotoxic activities of bovine seminal ribonuclease11 and Onconase.12 The use of site-directed mutagenesis and broad-spectrum inhibitors such as ribonuclease inhibitor (RI) protein13 have been invaluable in establishing the links between biological and enzymatic activities. However, the development of stable, low-molecular weight inhibitors with high specificity remains a priority for the study of individual enzymes in their natural settings. Furthermore, such compounds may lead to agents for the treatment of pathologies associated with ribonuclease action, most notably anti-tumor agents directed at Ang.8
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 97 99 97 99 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b14">14</xref>
###xml 278 279 278 279 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 282 283 282 283 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 290 291 290 291 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 440 442 440 442 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b14">14</xref>
###xml 443 445 443 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b15">15</xref>
###xml 685 687 685 687 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b16">16</xref>
###xml 939 940 939 940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 940 941 940 941 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 954 956 954 956 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;8</sup>
###xml 959 961 959 961 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;6</sup>
###xml 961 962 961 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 1004 1006 1004 1006 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b17">17</xref>
###xml 1007 1009 1007 1009 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b18">18</xref>
###xml 1109 1110 1109 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1110 1111 1110 1111 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1122 1123 1121 1122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 1170 1171 1169 1170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 1177 1179 1176 1178 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b19">19</xref>
RNase A superfamily members cleave the P-O5' bonds of RNA specifically after pyrimidine residues.14 Inhibition of this action with small molecules has focused principally on the central catalytic and substrate-binding region. This is conventionally divided into subsites named P1, B1, and B2, which bind the scissile bond and the heterocyclic bases immediately upstream (a pyrimidine) and downstream (preferentially a purine), respectively.14,15 One well-established line of attack involves phosphoadenosine-based nucleotides. Such compounds inhibit a variety of ribonucleases including RNase A, EDN, eosinophil cationic protein (ECP), RNase 4, Ang and, in all likelihood, many others.16 The tightest-binding examples reported thus far are chemically-synthesized derivatives of adenosine 5'-pyrophosphate (ppA); among these, 5'-diphosphoadenosine 3'-phosphate (ppA-3'-p) and its 5'-phospho 2'-deoxyuridine derivative (pdUppA-3'-p) exhibit Ki values of 10-8-10-6M when binding to RNase A, EDN, or RNase 4.17,18 This has been matched only by oligo (vinylsulfonic acid), a polyanion that inhibits RNase A with a Ki of 0.12 muM under similar buffer conditions containing 0.1M NaCl.19
###end p 8

###xml 1707 1708 1703 1704 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8242;</bold>
###xml 1710 1715 1706 1707 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</sub>
###xml 1706 1715 1702 1707 <td xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" align="center" rowspan="1" colspan="1">5<bold>&#8242;</bold>-P<sub>&#945;</sub></td>

In RNA, &#967; is usually <italic>anti</italic> (180&#8211;250&#176;) or high-<italic>anti</italic> (above 250&#176;) but rarely <italic>syn</italic> (&lt;120&#176;).<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="b30">30</xref>,<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="b31">31</xref></p></fn><fn id="tf1-3"><label>c</label><p textid="13">Letters in parentheses denote alternate ligand conformations.</p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
X-ray crystallographic studies of complexes formed between phosphoadenosine-based inhibitors and RNase A,20-22 EDN,23,24 and ECP25 have shown that these compounds bind minimally to the P1 and B2 subsites but can also make additional interactions further afield depending on the nature of substitution. Exploration of the more peripheral interactions may lead to the development of inhibitors that are specific to particular ribonuclease homologs. However, these enzyme.inhibitor systems exhibit remarkable conformational complexity and the confidence with which inhibitor improvements can be derived from the existing data is not high. For example, with the RNase A.inhibitor system (which has received most attention thus far; Table I), a simple RNA-derived compound such as pA-3'-p binds in the conventional manner observed for oligonucleotide substrate analogues32-35 (here designated as Class Ia) but a radically altered mode is observed upon modification of the compound with phosphate groups at the 5'- and/or 2'- positions. The two key torsional parameters that characterize this are the rotameric state of His119 (a residue that contributes to both the P1 and B2 subsites) and the N-glycosidic torsion angle (chi) of the nucleotide. These reflect to a large degree the nature of the base-stacking interaction at the B2 subsite and the region of the inhibitor that occupies the P1 subsite. ###xml 96 100 92 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">anti</italic>

###begin p 14
###xml 318 320 318 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b36">36</xref>
###xml 343 344 343 344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 344 345 344 345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sup>
###xml 346 347 346 347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 347 348 347 348 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sup>
###xml 382 383 382 383 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 402 403 402 403 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 536 537 536 537 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
In view of the conformational uncertainties in the binding of adenylic nucleotides, it remains a priority to extend the panel of inhibitor complexes for which structural data is available. It is pertinent that several naturally-occuring nucleotides that possess a ppA moiety are also effective ribonuclease inhibitors.36 These include 5'-ATP, P1,P3-bis(5'-adenosyl) triphosphate (Ap3A), NADPH, and NADP+. We present here the X-ray crystal structures of these compounds in complex with RNase A, along with that of a pyrophosphate ion (PPi) complex of the same. They provide new insight into the consequences of a variety of 5'-linked extensions on the binding of adenylic nucleotides to RNase A and its homologs, and indicate how improved inhibitors might be developed.
###end p 14

RESULTS
###end title 15
###begin title 16
Structural Overview
###end title 16
###begin p 17
###xml 68 69 68 69 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 83 84 83 84 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 92 93 92 93 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 194 196 194 196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">II</xref>
###xml 285 287 285 287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b20">20</xref>
###xml 321 322 321 322 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 815 820 815 816 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</sup>
###xml 944 946 940 942 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b20">20</xref>
###xml 976 977 972 973 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>

<italic>F</italic><sub>o</sub> and <italic>F</italic><sub>c</sub> are the observed and calculated structure factor amplitudes of reflection <italic>h</italic>, respectively.</p></fn><fn id="tf2-4"><label>d</label><p textid="22"><italic>R</italic><sub>free</sub> is equal to <italic>R</italic><sub>cryst</sub> for a randomly selected 5&#8211;10% of reflections not used in the refinement.<sup>37</sup></p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
The structures of monoclinic RNase A crystals soaked with 5'-ATP, Ap3A, NADPH, NADP+, and PPi were obtained at resolutions of 1.7, 2.4, 1.7, 1.7, and 1.8 A, respectively, as summarized in Table II. This crystal form presents two protein chains (mol A and mol B) in the asymmetric unit,20 and, with the exception of the Ap3A complex, which lacks residue LysA1, each of the structures comprises two complete main chains (residues 1-124). Density for residues 16-24 and 87-90 of each chain is consistently poor, as is typical for this crystal form. In Ramachandran plots, 94.2-96.7% of non-Pro/Gly residues lie in the most-favored regions with only SerB16 falling in a disfavored region. In no case is the main chain topology perturbed significantly by the presence of the ligand; of the 10 protein chains, nine have Calpha traces that deviate by 0.21-0.25 A (r.m.s.) from the corresponding chain in monoclinic unliganded RNase A (PDB entry 1AFU),20 whereas for chain A of the Ap3A complex, the figure is slightly higher at 0.48 A and appears to be a consequence of the relatively low resolution of this structure. ###xml 0 1 0 1 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 1 5 1 5 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">symm</sub>
###xml 13 14 9 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">h</italic>
###xml 13 14 9 10 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>h</italic></sub>

###xml 31 32 23 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>

###xml 50 51 34 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 51 52 35 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</italic>
###xml 51 52 35 36 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>i</italic></sub>
###xml 53 54 37 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">h</italic>
###xml 64 65 48 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 65 66 49 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</italic>
###xml 65 66 49 50 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>i</italic></sub>
###xml 74 75 58 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</italic>
###xml 95 96 79 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 97 98 81 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">h</italic>
###xml 145 146 129 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 147 148 131 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">h</italic>
Rsymm = SigmahSigmai[|Ii(h) - <I(h)>|/SigmahSigmaiIi(h)], where Ii is the ith measurement and <I(h)> is the weighted mean of all measurements of I(h).
###end p 19
###begin p 20
Values in parentheses refer to the outermost shell.
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 0 1 0 1 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 1 6 1 6 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cryst</sub>

###xml 19 20 15 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 20 21 16 17 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</sub>
###xml 28 29 20 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">h</italic>
###xml 28 29 20 21 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>h</italic></sub>
###xml 29 30 21 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 30 31 22 23 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">o</sub>
###xml 39 40 31 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 40 41 32 33 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">o</sub>
###xml 46 47 38 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 47 48 39 40 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</sub>
###xml 123 124 115 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">h</italic>
Rcryst = Sigmah|Fo-Fc|/SigmahFo, where Fo and Fc are the observed and calculated structure factor amplitudes of reflection h, respectively.
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 0 1 0 1 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 1 5 1 5 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">free</sub>
###xml 18 19 18 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 19 24 19 24 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cryst</sub>
###xml 97 99 97 99 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">37</sup>
Rfree is equal to Rcryst for a randomly selected 5-10% of reflections not used in the refinement.37
###end p 22

###xml 1519 1519 1515 1515 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="bip0091-0995-f2"/>
###xml 1037 1519 1037 1515 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="fig02" position="float"><label>FIGURE 2</label><caption><p textid="25">Electron density maps for the nucleotide inhibitors. Shown in stereo for (a) 5&#8242;-ATP (mol A), (b) Ap<sub>3</sub>A (mol A), (c) NADPH (mol A), (d) NADP<sup>+</sup> (mol A), and (e) PP<sub>i</sub> (mol B) is the ball-and-stick structure of the refined inhibitor (or fragment thereof) superposed with the corresponding portion of the total OMIT map calculated with SFCHECK<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="b62">62</xref> and contoured at 1.3&#963;. The coloring scheme is: carbon, gold; nitrogen, blue; oxygen, red; phosphorus, pink; electron density, green.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="bip0091-0995-f2"/></fig>
Chemical structures, harmonized atom nomenclature, and conserved torsion angles of the nucleotide inhibitors are presented in Figure 1. For each of these compounds, the electron density data indicate clearly the position of one adenine ring and 2-3 phosphate groups but not that of the intervening ribosyl moiety (Figure 2). This parallels the difficulty experienced in locating the ribosyl backbone atoms in many RNA structures.38 Plausible coordinates were derived through crystallographic refinement with REFMAC539 with referral to the all-atom contact analysis of MolProbity40 and in the knowledge that the lever-actions of the base and phosphates dictate to a large degree the sugar's conformation.41 The position of each of the nucleotide inhibitors is better defined in mol A than in mol B. In several cases, this may be due to the stabilizing influence of a crystal contact, as described in more detail below. FIGURE 1Chemical structures, harmonized atom numbering, and conserved torsion angles of 5'-ATP, Ap3A, NADPH, and NADP+.FIGURE 2Electron density maps for the nucleotide inhibitors. Shown in stereo for (a) 5'-ATP (mol A), (b) Ap3A (mol A), (c) NADPH (mol A), (d) NADP+ (mol A), and (e) PPi (mol B) is the ball-and-stick structure of the refined inhibitor (or fragment thereof) superposed with the corresponding portion of the total OMIT map calculated with SFCHECK62 and contoured at 1.3sigma. The coloring scheme is: carbon, gold; nitrogen, blue; oxygen, red; phosphorus, pink; electron density, green.
###end p 23

align="center" rowspan="1" colspan="1">&#8212;</td><td align="center" rowspan="1" colspan="1">&#8212;</td></tr></tbody></table><table-wrap-foot><fn id="tf4-1"><label>a</label><p textid="34">Potential hydrogen bonds are listed if identified with HBPLUS<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="b44">44</xref> and corroborated by clear electron density for donor and acceptor.</p></fn><fn id="tf4-2"><label>b</label><p textid="35">Crystal contact with symmetry-related mol B.</p></fn><fn id="tf4-3"><label>c</label><p textid="36">Distance exceeds normal limits but is included for comparison.</p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
The inhibition of RNase A by simple 5'-phosphorylated adenosines becomes progressively stronger as the number of phosphates is increased. Under equivalent conditions, Ki values for 5'-AMP (pA), 5'-ADP (ppA), and 5'-ATP (pppA) are 80, 1.2, and 0.86 muM, respectively.18,36 The 67-fold drop in Ki experienced when moving from 5'-AMP to 5'-ADP coincides with a radical change in nucleotide conformation (Class Ia/Ib to Class II; Table I).22,26 We now present the crystal structure of the RNase A.5'-ATP complex. The electron density map indicates the position of the base, the beta- and the gamma-phosphate but there is significant disorder in between (Figure 2a). The adenine ring is positioned as in the 5'-AMP complex, stacking with His119 (rotamer A) and hydrogen-bonding with Asn71 in a conventional (Class Ia) fashion, but a small decrease in chi coupled with a pronounced curvature of the triphosphate chain brings the gamma- rather than the alpha-phosphate into the P1 subsite (Figure 3; Table III). As such, the binding mode conforms to Class Ib. The two instances of the inhibitor in the asymmetric unit show modest differences in their ribose and triphosphate conformations that permit alternative hydrogen-bonding arrangements. Bonds are consistently made between the gamma-phosphate and His12, His119, and Phe120 but involve different inhibitor atoms (Table IV). Also, whereas in mol A there are two potential hydrogen bonds between the beta-phosphate and Gln11, in mol B there is one between the gamma-phosphate and this residue. There are no direct interactions between the inhibitor and symmetry-related protein atoms that might explain the differences, and the underlying cause is not clear. Water-mediated interactions are made with Gln11, Asn67, Val118 (mol A only), Phe120 (mol A only), and Asp121, while Coulombic interactions link the Nzeta atom of Lys7 (a component of the P2 subsite) and the polyphosphate chain, the closest approach being 3.6 A to the beta-phosphate in mol A. ###begin p 37
###xml 301 304 297 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">syn</italic>
###xml 378 379 371 372 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 582 583 575 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 583 584 576 577 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 802 804 792 794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b21">21</xref>
###xml 905 909 891 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">anti</italic>
5'-ATP is the first compound containing a gamma-phosphate group for which the three-dimensional details of RNase A binding have been obtained. Previous studies on adenylic nucleotides that contain a 5'-pyrophosphate group (in various states of derivatization) are consistent in their description of a syn base conformation and in their placement of beta-phosphate as the major P1 subsite ligand when bound to RNase A (Class II binding). The conformation observed here for RNase A-bound 5'-ATP represents a deviation from this pattern and offers an explanation for the stagnation in Ki encountered when moving from 5'-ADP to 5'-ATP. That is, although the Class II binding mode can support productive interactions of additional 5'-beta-phosphate-linked substituents (e.g., in the binding of pdUppA-3'-p),21 with 5'-ATP these are not as favorable as those involving the gamma-phosphate after adoption of the anti conformation observed here.
###end p 37
###begin p 38
###xml 72 73 60 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 73 74 61 62 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 82 83 69 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 85 87 72 74 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b36">36</xref>
###xml 151 153 138 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b24">24</xref>
###xml 374 375 361 362 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
5'-ATP also inhibits EDN, albeit approximately25-fold less effectively (Ki = 21 muM).36 The manner in which this compound binds to EDN (PDB entry 2C01)24 differs from that observed here with RNase A. A mixture of two conformations is present, neither of which is particularly well ordered. In one of these (conformation A), the adenine ring is bound as in RNase A, but the P1 subsite is occupied principally by the alpha-phosphate whereas the gamma-phosphate is disordered. The catalytic centers of the two proteins are highly similar, and it seems that electronic and/or steric effects of a subtle nature are responsible for the differences in binding. Whatever the case, the superior inhibition of RNase A correlates with a better-defined and more extensive interaction between inhibitor and protein.
###end p 38

Extension of 5'-ATP by attachment of a 5'-linked adenosine, thereby generating Ap3A (Figure 1), causes a 34-fold decrease in affinity (Ki = 29 muM).36 To find an explanation, we determined the structure of the RNase A.Ap3A complex. The electron density map indicates the position of a portion of the nucleotide corresponding to a 5'-ATP moiety (Figure 2b), and the remainder of the inhibitor is presumed to be in no fixed conformation. The visible portion has the adenine/His119 rotamer A stacking arrangement and syn base conformation of the Class II binding mode associated with 5'-pyrophosphate-containing adenine nucleotides (Figure 4a; Table III). There are modest differences in the binding of the inhibitor to the two protein chains in the asymmetric unit. These appear to derive from a hydrogen bond in mol A between O2' of the ribose and Ogamma1 of a symmetry-related ThrB70 residue. This has negligible impact on the adenine position but alters the conformation of the ribose and, to a lesser degree, the polyphosphate chain (Table III). Two hydrogen bonds between the adenine and the side chain of Asn71 are maintained, as is one between the beta-phosphate and His12, and one between the gamma-phosphate and Lys41 (Table IV). The Nzeta atom of Lys7 is approximately 4 A away from the alpha-phosphate, close enough for significant Coulombic interactions. Differences between the two instances of the inhibitor include a hydrogen bond between the alpha-phosphate and His119 in mol A only and one between the beta-phosphate and Phe120 in mol B only. FIGURE 4RNase A.Ap3A complex (mol A). (a) Enzyme and inhibitor in the same representation and orientation as in Figure 3. The inhibitor is disordered beyond the 5'-gamma-phosphate. (b) Comparison with the EDN.Ap3A complex (PDB entry 2C02).24 The two complexes were superposed on the basis of the Calpha positions of key nucleotide-binding residues (from RNase A, mol A: Q11, H12, K41, T45, H119, and F120; from EDN: Q14, H15, K38, T42, H129, and L130). Shown in stereo in the same orientation as in panel a are ball-and-stick representations of RNase A-bound Ap3A (colored as in panel a), EDN-bound Ap3A (white), and neighboring EDN residues (green), along with a surface representation of EDN. Main chain N, C, and O atoms of residues W10, Q14, H15, K38, Q40, and D112 are omitted for clarity. The EDN-bound inhibitor is disordered beyond the 5'-beta-phosphate.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 10 11 10 11 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 111 112 111 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">3</xref>
###xml 203 204 199 200 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 231 233 227 229 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b24">24</xref>
###xml 289 294 285 286 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</sup>
###xml 553 554 545 546 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 593 594 585 586 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>

###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 111 112 111 112 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 326 327 322 323 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 436 437 432 433 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">3</xref>
###xml 589 591 585 587 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b21">21</xref>
###xml 750 751 746 747 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
Although they comprise the same set of atoms, RNase A-bound 5'-ATP and the ordered portion of likewise-bound Ap3A exhibit conformations that are clearly very different from one another. In the 5'-ATP complex, the compact conformation of the polyphosphate chain and the tendency of the gamma-phosphate toward burial among the P1 subsite residues appears to leave little scope for the addition of a second 5'-linked adenosine (see Figure 3). A switch to the Class II binding mode, however, provides an exit route for the 5'-extension, as is observed for other inhibitors such as pdUppA-3'-p.21 The loss of 1-2 hydrogen bonds that accompanies this change most likely contributes to the decrease in affinity that is observed when moving from 5'-ATP to Ap3A.
###end p 42
###begin p 43
###xml 2 3 2 3 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 42 43 42 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 43 44 43 44 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 52 53 51 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 55 57 54 56 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b36">36</xref>
###xml 93 95 92 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b24">24</xref>
###xml 174 177 173 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">syn</italic>
###xml 384 385 383 384 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig04">4</xref>
###xml 456 457 448 449 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 562 564 554 556 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b24">24</xref>
Ap3A inhibits EDN with a similar potency (Ki = 70 muM).36 When bound to EDN (PDB entry 2C02),24 the conformation of the second adenosine moiety is likewise disordered, but a syn base conformation is not observed. The reason for this is the need to avoid an overlap between the O3' edge of the ribose and the side chain of Trp7 (a residue whose counterpart in RNase A is Ala4) (Figure 4b). The alpha- and beta-phosphates appear to hydrogen-bond with EDN's P1 subsite but it was not possible to arrive at a definitive arrangement due to disorder in the nucleotide.24 It seems likely that hydrogen-bonding is less extensive than in the RNase A complex and that this is compensated for by the adoption of a more favorable base conformation to give a similar binding affinity.
###end p 43
###begin title 44
###xml 48 49 48 49 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
Structures of the RNase A.NADPH and RNase A.NADP+ Complexes
###end title 44
###begin p 45
###xml 78 79 78 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 79 80 79 80 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 90 91 89 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 93 95 92 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b18">18</xref>
###xml 110 111 109 110 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 230 231 229 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 231 232 230 231 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 255 256 253 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 271 273 269 271 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b36">36</xref>
###xml 352 353 350 351 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
The compound ppA-2'-p is among the tightest-binding RNase A inhibitors known (Ki = 0.52 muM).18 NADPH and NADP+ are naturally-occurring substances that contain a ppA-2'-p moiety yet are considerably less effective inhibitors with Ki values of 12 and 63 muM, respectively.36 Seeking an explanation, we determined the crystal structures of NADPH and NADP+ in complex with RNase A. These reveal no major differences between the binding of the two inhibitors and therefore they will be treated together.
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 214 215 211 212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig02">2</xref>
###xml 221 222 218 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig02">2</xref>
###xml 312 313 309 310 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 330 331 327 328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">5</xref>
###xml 478 480 475 477 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b22">22</xref>
###xml 481 483 478 480 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b23">23</xref>
###xml 484 486 481 483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b45">45</xref>
###xml 717 723 714 716 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#947;1</sup>
###xml 794 795 787 788 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 936 939 929 932 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="tbl3">III</xref>
###xml 1211 1212 1204 1205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">5</xref>
###xml 1220 1222 1213 1215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="tbl4">IV</xref>
###xml 1373 1377 1366 1367 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#950;</sup>
###xml 1768 1776 1750 1758 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FIGURE 5</label>
###xml 1894 1895 1876 1877 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">3</xref>
###xml 1776 2109 1758 2087 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="47">RNase A&#183;NADPH complex (mol A). The side chains of V43 and E111 are drawn in dual conformation (as fitted to the electron density) whereas the side chain of V118 is omitted for clarity. The inhibitor is disordered beyond the 5&#8242;-&#945;-phosphate.</p>
###xml 1776 2109 1758 2087 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="47">RNase A&#183;NADPH complex (mol A). Shown are enzyme and inhibitor in the same representation and orientation as in Figure <xref ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">3</xref>. The side chains of V43 and E111 are drawn in dual conformation (as fitted to the electron density) whereas the side chain of V118 is omitted for clarity. The inhibitor is disordered beyond the 5&#8242;-&#945;-phosphate.</p></caption>
###xml 2109 2109 2087 2087 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="bip0091-0995-f5"/>
###xml 1768 2109 1750 2087 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="fig05" position="float"><label>FIGURE 5</label><caption><p textid="47">RNase A&#183;NADPH complex (mol A). Shown are enzyme and inhibitor in the same representation and orientation as in Figure <xref ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">3</xref>. The side chains of V43 and E111 are drawn in dual conformation (as fitted to the electron density) whereas the side chain of V118 is omitted for clarity. The inhibitor is disordered beyond the 5&#8242;-&#945;-phosphate.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="bip0091-0995-f5"/></fig>
The electron density map permits modelling of a pA-2'-p moiety; no density is observed for the 5'-beta-phosphate, nicotinamide or the intervening sugar and they are presumed to be in no fixed conformation (Figures 2c and 2d). The adenine ring stacks against His119 (rotamer B) and the 2'-phosphate occupies the P1 subsite (Figure 5). This conforms to Class III binding and matches the mode reported for pA-2'-p bound to crystalline RNase A (mol A) and EDN or to Ang in solution.22,23,45 Again, there are small conformational differences between the binding of the inhibitor to each of the two protein chains in the asymmetric unit. These appear to stem from a hydrogen bond in mol A between adenine atom N6 and atom Ogamma1 of a symmetry-related ThrB70 residue (the same residue that affects Ap3A binding). This brings about a 3.4-A shift in the position of atom N6 and compensatory adjustments to the remainder of the inhibitor (Table III). However, it has minimal effect on the 2'-phosphate group, which is particularly well ordered in the electron density map, suggesting that it is the main focal point for binding. The 2'-phosphate hydrogen-bonds with His12, His119, Phe120, and Gln11 (mol B only) (Figure 5, Table IV). There are also water-mediated interactions between the inhibitor and Gln11, Lys41, Gln69, Asp121, Val118 (mol A only), and Asn71 (mol B only). The Nzeta atom of Lys7 is roughly equidistant from the 2'- and 5'-alpha-phosphate groups; at 5.8-6.6 A away, it is somewhat more remote than in the other complexes described in this report. The 5'-alpha-phosphate makes no hydrogen-bonding interactions with the protein and is oriented toward the solvent, indicating that the nicotinamide nucleotide portion is in a disordered, solvent-exposed state. FIGURE 5RNase A.NADPH complex (mol A). Shown are enzyme and inhibitor in the same representation and orientation as in Figure 3. The side chains of V43 and E111 are drawn in dual conformation (as fitted to the electron density) whereas the side chain of V118 is omitted for clarity. The inhibitor is disordered beyond the 5'-alpha-phosphate.
###end p 46
###begin p 47
###xml 118 119 118 119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">3</xref>
RNase A.NADPH complex (mol A). Shown are enzyme and inhibitor in the same representation and orientation as in Figure 3. The side chains of V43 and E111 are drawn in dual conformation (as fitted to the electron density) whereas the side chain of V118 is omitted for clarity. The inhibitor is disordered beyond the 5'-alpha-phosphate.
###end p 47
###begin p 48
###xml 126 127 126 127 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 166 167 166 167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 167 168 167 168 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 300 302 300 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b23">23</xref>
###xml 307 309 307 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b25">25</xref>
###xml 317 319 317 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b45">45</xref>
###xml 320 322 320 322 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b46">46</xref>
###xml 392 393 392 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 393 394 393 394 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 403 404 402 403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 406 408 405 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b18">18</xref>
###xml 595 596 594 595 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 706 707 705 706 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 800 802 799 801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b36">36</xref>
Given the similarity between the interactions of RNase A (mol A)-bound pA-2'-p and those of the visible portions of NADPH/NADP+, one might expect a correspondence in Ki values. The literature contains no inhibition constant for the RNase A.pA-2'-p interaction, but structural and kinetic data on EDN,23 ECP,25 and Ang45,46 indicate that it will be in the region of that measured for pA-3'-p (Ki = 4.7 muM),18 which is indeed similar to that reported for NADPH. The present data do not provide a structural basis for the 5-fold decrease in affinity that is measured when moving from NADPH to NADP+. It seems most likely that this is related to electrostatic repulsion of the cationic pyridinium ring of NADP+ by the surplus of positive charge in the active site of the enzyme, as suggested previously.36
###end p 48
###begin p 49
###xml 28 29 28 29 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 134 137 134 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">syn</italic>
###xml 220 222 220 222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b20">20</xref>
###xml 468 470 465 467 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">20</sup>
###xml 573 575 570 572 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b21">21</xref>
Although both NADPH and NADP+ contain ppA-2'-p as a structural element, the adenylic portions of these dinucleotides do not adopt the syn base (Class II) conformation observed when ppA-2'-p binds to RNase A in isolation.20 It is possible that the position and orientation observed for the 5'-beta-phosphate group of enzyme-bound ppA-2'-p leave no room for accommodation of an adjacent ribosyl group. This differs from the corresponding portion of enzyme-bound ppA-3'-p20 which has been shown to offer access to additional 5'-linked substituents, e.g., those in pdUppA-3'-p.21
###end p 49
###begin title 50
###xml 27 28 27 28 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
Structure of the RNase A.PPi Complex
###end title 50
###begin p 51
###xml 171 172 171 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 172 173 172 173 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 194 195 181 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 197 199 184 186 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b47">47</xref>
###xml 309 310 296 297 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 392 393 379 380 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig02">2</xref>
###xml 508 509 495 496 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig06">6</xref>
###xml 694 702 677 679 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#603;2</sup>
###xml 711 719 688 690 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#603;2</sup>
###xml 729 735 700 702 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#948;1</sup>
###xml 797 801 764 765 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#950;</sup>
###xml 899 903 860 861 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#950;</sup>
###xml 947 948 905 906 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1028 1036 986 988 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#603;2</sup>
###xml 1164 1172 1102 1110 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FIGURE 6</label>
###xml 1182 1183 1120 1121 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1305 1306 1243 1244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">3</xref>
###xml 1338 1339 1276 1277 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1365 1367 1303 1305 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b49">49</xref>
###xml 1423 1428 1361 1362 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</sup>
###xml 1688 1689 1622 1623 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1727 1728 1661 1662 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1172 1943 1110 1877 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="52">RNase A&#183;PP<sub>i</sub> complex (mol B). ###xml 1172 1943 1110 1877 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="52">RNase A&#183;PP<sub>i</sub> complex (mol B). ###xml 1943 1943 1877 1877 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="bip0091-0995-f6"/>
###xml 1164 1943 1102 1877 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="fig06" position="float"><label>FIGURE 6</label><caption><p textid="52">RNase A&#183;PP<sub>i</sub> complex (mol B). (a) Enzyme and inhibitor in the same representation and approximately the same orientation as in Figure <xref ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">3</xref>. (b) Comparison with the Ang&#183;PP<sub>i</sub> complex (PDB entry 1H52).<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="b49">49</xref> The two complexes were superposed on the basis of the C<sup>&#945;</sup> positions of key nucleotide-binding residues (from RNase A, mol B: Q11, H12, K41, T45, H119, and F120; from Ang: Q12, H13, K40, T44, H114, and L115). Shown in stereo from the same viewpoint as for panel a are ball-and-stick representations of RNase A-bound PP<sub>i</sub> (colored as in panel a), Ang-bound PP<sub>i</sub> (white), and neighboring Ang residues (green), along with a surface representation of Ang. Main chain N, C, and O atoms of residues H8, Q12, H13, and K40 are omitted for clarity. Dashed lines denote hydrogen bonds.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="bip0091-0995-f6"/></fig>
A pyrophosphate moiety is an invariant substituent of the most potent nucleotide-based inhibitors identified to date. Even as a free ion, it inhibits RNase A appreciably (Ki approximately 170 muM),47 highlighting its contribution to the affinity of these inhibitors. In the crystal structure of the RNase A.PPi complex, electron density for the ion is clear, particularly so in mol B (Figure 2e). Both halves of the ion interact with the protein via multiple direct and water-mediated hydrogen bonds (Figure 6a). There is very little difference between the two instances of the ion in the asymmetric unit. One half of the ion (which we designate the alpha-phosphate) hydrogen-bonds with Gln11 Nepsilon2, His12 Nepsilon2, His119 Ndelta1, and Phe120 N and experiences Coulombic attraction to Lys 7 Nzeta, which is at a distance of 5.2 A. The other half (the beta-phosphate) hydrogen-bonds with Lys41 Nzeta and Phe120 O (provided that the relevant PPi oxygen is protonated). Water-mediated hydrogen bonds are also made with Gln11 Nepsilon2 (alpha-phosphate), Val43 O (beta-phosphate, mol B only), Thr45 N (beta-phosphate), and Val118 O (alpha-phosphate, mol A only). FIGURE 6RNase A.PPi complex (mol B). (a) Enzyme and inhibitor in the same representation and approximately the same orientation as in Figure 3. (b) Comparison with the Ang.PPi complex (PDB entry 1H52).49 The two complexes were superposed on the basis of the Calpha positions of key nucleotide-binding residues (from RNase A, mol B: Q11, H12, K41, T45, H119, and F120; from Ang: Q12, H13, K40, T44, H114, and L115). Shown in stereo from the same viewpoint as for panel a are ball-and-stick representations of RNase A-bound PPi (colored as in panel a), Ang-bound PPi (white), and neighboring Ang residues (green), along with a surface representation of Ang. Main chain N, C, and O atoms of residues H8, Q12, H13, and K40 are omitted for clarity. Dashed lines denote hydrogen bonds.
###end p 51
###begin p 52
###xml 10 11 10 11 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
