###begin p 53
###xml 146 148 138 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b22">22</xref>
###xml 149 151 141 143 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b34">34</xref>
###xml 304 306 293 295 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b20">20</xref>
###xml 307 309 296 298 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b21">21</xref>
###xml 484 485 466 467 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 503 504 485 486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig04">4</xref>
###xml 534 535 516 517 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
The position of the alpha-phosphate is a good match to that of a conventionally-bound 5'-alpha-phosphate such as that present in pA-3'-p or d(CpA)22,34 and is an approximate match to that of the 5'-beta-phosphate present in ppA-3'-p, ppA-2'-p or 3',5'-pyrophosphate-linked inhibitors such as pdUppA-3'-p.20,21 The position of the beta-phosphate does not correspond well with that of any phosphate group among known inhibitors. It is closest to that of the 5'-gamma-phosphate in the Ap3A complex (Figure 4a) but is further toward the B1 subsite.
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 29 30 29 30 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 221 222 221 222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b8">8</xref>
###xml 478 479 478 479 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 488 490 488 490 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b48">48</xref>
###xml 572 573 572 573 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 578 580 578 580 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b49">49</xref>
###xml 661 662 661 662 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 812 813 812 813 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig06">6</xref>
###xml 1067 1072 1064 1065 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#947;</sup>
###xml 1357 1358 1335 1336 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1368 1369 1346 1347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1369 1370 1347 1348 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1378 1379 1356 1357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 1381 1383 1359 1361 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b49">49</xref>
The details of the RNase A.PPi structure aid in the interpretation of the nucleotide-binding properties of the homologous ribonuclease, Ang. Inhibitors of Ang have potential therapeutic use as anti-cancer drugs (reference8 and others therein) but their binding has proved to be far less amenable to crystallographic study owing to the obstructive position of symmetry-related molecules in all crystal forms identified to date and, in some cases, to the cryptic nature of Ang's B1 subsite.48 The largest entity that has been observed bound to the active site of Ang is a PPi ion.49 This binds in a position that is very similar to that observed in the RNase A.PPi complex, with Ang residues Gln12, His13, His114, and Leu115 substituting for RNase A residues Gln11, His12, His119, and Phe120, respectively (Figure 6b). The main difference between the two complexes is the rotameric state of the beta-phosphate, which permits a hydrogen bond with Lys41 in RNase A but not with its counterpart (Lys40) in Ang. The most likely cause is the need to avert a clash with the Cgamma atom of Gln117 (a component of the novel C-terminal segment of Ang) which, when superposed, is located approximately 2.5 A from the position occupied by one of the beta-phosphate oxygens in the RNase A complex. The loss of this hydrogen bond may contribute to the lower affinity of PPi for Ang (Ki = 1.7 mM).49
###end p 54
###begin title 55
DISCUSSION
###end title 55
###begin title 56
Use of Monoclinic RNase A Crystals in the Study of Inhibitor Binding
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 22 24 22 24 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b20">20</xref>
###xml 260 262 260 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b16">16</xref>
###xml 305 306 305 306 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 308 309 308 309 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 311 312 311 312 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 462 464 462 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b21">21</xref>
###xml 670 671 670 671 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1229 1231 1229 1231 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b22">22</xref>
###xml 1232 1234 1232 1234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b27">27</xref>
###xml 1375 1376 1375 1376 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1392 1393 1392 1393 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
Since their discovery,20 monoclinic RNase A crystals have proven to be well suited to the study and development of ribonuclease inhibitors. In their favor, they grow at low ionic strength and moderate acidity, both of which are conducive to nucleotide binding.16 They also offer good access to the whole B1-P1-B2 region of each of the protein molecules in the asymmetric unit, as indicated by the excellent electron density observed for enzyme-bound pdUppA-3'-p.21 The quality of the present structures supports the utility of these crystals but reaffirms one drawback, namely the potential impact of symmetry-related protein chains on the binding of inhibitors to the B2 subsite. Mol A is the most affected owing to potential direct hydrogen-bonding interactions between the inhibitor and a symmetry-related ThrB70 residue and, to a lesser degree, to constrainment of GluA111 by its packing against a symmetry-related TyrB115 residue. In addition, GlnA69 and GlnB69 pack against one another, which could conceivably constrain either residue. These features do not affect the overall binding mode or conformational order of the present inhibitors but they have been seen to do so, for example in the binding of pA-2'-p and dUppA.22,27 In those cases where there is a degree of conformational disorder and an ensemble of inhibitor conformations exists (e.g., the binding of Ap3A, NADPH or NADP+), the symmetry-related contacts of mol A might be viewed as a helpful means of selecting a representative conformation, but it may be that mol B is a more reliable indicator of solution behavior.
###end p 57
###begin title 58
Prospects for Improved Adenylic Inhibitors of RNase A
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 235 236 224 225 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 320 321 309 310 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 435 436 424 425 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 454 455 443 444 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 610 611 599 600 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 834 835 823 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</italic>
###xml 835 840 824 825 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#189;</sub>
###xml 876 877 855 856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 885 887 864 866 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b50">50</xref>
###xml 1056 1057 1035 1036 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1151 1153 1130 1132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b51">51</xref>
###xml 1154 1156 1133 1135 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b52">52</xref>
The conformational diversity of RNase A-bound adenylic inhibitors continues to expand. With our report of the RNase A.5'-ATP structure, there are now accounts of the binding of 5'-alpha-, 5'-beta-, 5'-gamma-, and 2'-phosphates to the P1 subsite. The torsional flexibility of the nucleotides and the adaptability of the B2 subsite are key factors. Despite the array of possible conformations, the larger inhibitors investigated here (Ap3A, NADPH, and NADP+) are only partially visible in their respective electron density maps. The possibility of nonenzymatic cleavage of these inhibitors must be considered. Ap3A is known to be susceptible to hydrolytic cleavage within the polyphosphate chain but the reaction yields products (5'-ADP and 5'-AMP) that are smaller than the visible moiety (5'-ATP) and occurs at an insignificant rate (t(1/2) = 154 d at 60degreesC, pH 6.0, and I = 0.1).50 For pyridine nucleotides under mildly acidic conditions, polyphosphate cleavage is not a significant form of degradation. It does occur with oxidized forms such as NADP+ but elevated temperatures and alkaline conditions are required for the detection of products.51,52 In view of this, the partial electron density observed in the present complexes most likely reflects a lack of interaction between one half of the dinucleotide and the protein. It appears that, as the complexity of the 5'-linked extension increases, the need to avoid unfavorable protein.inhibitor contacts becomes an overiding influence on the binding mode and a reduced number of modes can support the binding of the compound.
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 32 33 32 33 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 51 52 51 52 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 101 102 101 102 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 110 111 110 111 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 120 122 120 122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b24">24</xref>
###xml 203 204 203 204 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sub>
###xml 397 398 397 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 398 399 398 399 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 454 455 454 455 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 458 459 458 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 459 460 459 460 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 468 469 467 468 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 481 482 480 481 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 485 486 484 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 486 487 485 486 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 496 497 494 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 504 505 502 503 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sub>
###xml 508 509 506 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 509 510 507 508 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 520 521 517 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 620 622 617 619 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b36">36</xref>
The incomplete interaction of Ap3A, NADPH, and NADP+ with RNase A is reminiscent of the binding of Ap3A and Ap4A to EDN.24 With the latter enzyme, further extension of the polyphosphate linker to form Ap5A brought about a far more extensive interaction, indicating that inclusion of an appropriate linker can have a dramatic effect on binding. Hence, it remains possible that the decreases in the Ki for RNase A inhibition encountered when moving from Ap3A (Ki = 29 muM) through Ap4A (Ki = 2.6 muM) to Ap5A (Ki = 0.23 muM) reflect the formation of new interactions permitted by linker extension, as previously suggested.36
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 33 34 33 34 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 272 273 272 273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">I</xref>
The details of the NADPH and NADP+ complexes give insight into the suitability of pA-2'-p or ppA-2'-p as a core for the development of larger inhibitors of RNase A. Although three different binding modes have been observed for 2'-phosphoadenosine-based nucleotides (Table I), none of these permits binding of the nicotinamide portion of the present nucleotides. As with the diadenosine polyphosphates, the inclusion of extended, unbranched linkers may be necessary to facilitate additional interactions beyond the 5'-beta-phosphate.
###end p 61
###begin title 62
Inhibitors of Specific Ribonuclease Subclasses
###end title 62
###begin p 63
###xml 352 354 352 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b53">53</xref>
###xml 455 456 455 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 456 457 456 457 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 538 540 538 540 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b16">16</xref>
###xml 854 855 854 855 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 866 867 866 867 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 879 881 879 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b49">49</xref>
###xml 921 922 921 922 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1165 1167 1165 1167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b45">45</xref>
###xml 1249 1250 1249 1250 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1261 1262 1261 1262 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 1473 1474 1473 1474 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
The development of inhibitors that are specific for individual ribonuclease subclasses would be of great value to the study of these enzymes in vivo and for the development of potential ribonuclease-directed therapeutics. High-throughput screening has identified several non-nucleotide inhibitors that bind slightly more tightly to Ang than to RNase A.53 Existing adenylic inhibitors, on the other hand, tend to select against Ang, for which they exhibit Ki values that are 2-3 orders of magnitude greater than those obtained for RNase A.16 With the nucleotides, the design process has been hampered by an inability to obtain Ang.inhibitor complexes in crystalline form and it has been necessary to extrapolate from data on RNase A and other enzymes. To help test the validity of these measures, a direct comparison can now be made between the RNase A.PPi and Ang.PPi structures.49 It is clear that the manner in which PPi binds to RNase A is not an accurate indicator of what occurs when the same group is O5'-linked to an adenylic nucleotide. The same is true for Ang, as can be deduced from heteronuclear NMR data on its interaction with ppA-2'-p and dUppA-2'-p.45 Although there is a close correspondence in the ligand position in the RNase A.PPi and Ang.PPi structures, there is a difference in the manner in which the two enzymes bind ppA-2'-p (Class II and Class III modes, respectively). Nevertheless, with the larger derivatives that have been examined (NADPH/NADP+ with RNase A and dUppA-2'-p with Ang), the Class III mode prevails (as does the nonengagement of the second nucleotide), suggesting that similar strategies may be necessary to improve the affinity of 2'-phosphoadenosine-based nucleotides for these enzymes.
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 192 194 192 194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b17">17</xref>
###xml 230 231 230 231 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 243 244 243 244 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 284 285 284 285 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig04">4</xref>
It has been suggested that side chain differences located toward the N-terminus of the protein could contribute to differences in the affinity of adenylic inhibitors for various ribonucleases.17 The contrast between the RNase A.Ap3A and EDN.Ap3A structures supports this view (Figure 4b). The complete conformational switch that is apparently triggered by the Trp7 side chain of EDN highlights that such steric effects can be strong and could be exploited in the inhibitor design process. In particular, the close proximity of Trp7 to the ribosyl O3' atom of the inhibitor suggests that O3'-linked substituents above a certain size may not be tolerated well by this enzyme and may disfavor binding.
###end p 64
###begin title 65
MATERIALS AND METHODS
###end title 65
###begin title 66
Crystallization and Data Collection
###end title 66
###begin p 67
###xml 42 43 42 43 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 57 58 57 58 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 66 67 66 67 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 226 228 220 222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b20">20</xref>
###xml 297 298 291 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 360 361 354 355 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 375 376 369 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 379 380 373 374 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 387 388 381 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 400 401 394 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 406 407 400 401 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 417 418 411 412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</italic>
###xml 421 422 415 416 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 531 532 519 520 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 540 541 528 529 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 675 676 663 664 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 776 777 764 765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 844 846 828 830 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b54">54</xref>
###xml 860 862 844 846 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b55">55</xref>
###xml 863 865 847 849 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b56">56</xref>
###xml 921 923 905 907 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">II</xref>
RNase A and the sodium salts of 5'-ATP, Ap3A, NADPH, NADP+, and PPi were obtained from Sigma and dissolved in water. RNase A crystals were grown at 16degreesC by the hanging-drop/vapor-diffusion method as described previously.20 These were transferred to a stabilizing solution (25% PEG 4000, 0.02M sodium citrate buffer, pH 5.5) supplemented with either 100 mM 5'-ATP, 100 mM Ap3A, 20 mM NADPH, 20 mM NADP+, or 100 mM PPi at 16degreesC for 24 h. Diffraction data were collected at 100 K; for crystals soaked in 5'-ATP, NADPH, NADP+, and PPi, this was carried out on stations 14.1, 9.6, 9.6, and 14.2 of the SRS, Daresbury, UK, respectively, whereas for crystals soaked in Ap3A, this was conducted in-house using a MAR Research 30-cm image plate mounted on a Rigaku RU-H3R Cu Kalpha radiation source. All data were processed using the HKL suite54 and TRUNCATE.55,56 Detailed data processing statistics are given in Table II.
###end p 67
###begin title 68
Phase Determination and Refinement
###end title 68
###begin p 69
###xml 80 82 80 82 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b57">57</xref>
###xml 213 215 213 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b20">20</xref>
###xml 323 324 323 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 358 360 358 360 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b58">58</xref>
###xml 423 425 423 425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b39">39</xref>
###xml 521 523 521 523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b37">37</xref>
###xml 656 658 656 658 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b59">59</xref>
###xml 659 661 659 661 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b60">60</xref>
###xml 724 725 724 725 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 725 726 725 726 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">o</sub>
###xml 728 729 728 729 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 729 730 729 730 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</sub>
###xml 814 816 814 816 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b61">61</xref>
###xml 864 865 864 865 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 865 866 865 866 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">o</sub>
###xml 868 869 868 869 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 869 870 869 870 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</sub>
###xml 1014 1016 1010 1012 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b40">40</xref>
###xml 1071 1073 1067 1069 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">II</xref>
Initial phases were determined using the molecular replacement routines of AMoRe57 with reference to coordinates of unliganded RNase A obtained previously under the same crystal growth conditions (PDB entry 1AFU).20 Refinement was conducted initially using the rigid-body, simulated annealing, coordinate minimization, and B-factor refinement elements of CNS58 and latterly using the maximum-likelihood routines of REFMAC5.39 Throughout, 5-10% of reflections (depending on resolution) were set aside for cross-validation.37 After every refinement cycle, electron density maps were calculated and used to guide manual adjustments made with either O or COOT.59,60 Ligands or fragments thereof were introduced on the basis of mFo-DFc maps and refined using geometrical restraints provided by the CCP4 monomer library.61 Water molecules were added at positions where mFo-DFc electron density peak heights exceeded 3sigma and where potential hydrogen bonds could be made. Model validation was conducted with MolProbity.40 Detailed statistics for each model are given in Table II.
###end p 69
###begin p 70
###xml 92 93 92 93 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 107 108 107 108 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 116 117 116 117 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
Data Deposition: The coordinates and structure factors of RNase A in complex with 5'-ATP, Ap3A, NADPH, NADP+, and PPi have been deposited in the Protein Data Bank under accession numbers 2W5G, 2W5I, 2W5K, 2W5L, and 2W5M, respectively.
###end p 70
